  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;
    background: 0;
    cursor: pointer;
  }
  h1, h2, h3, h4 {
    background: none;

  a, chops-button, a.button, .button, .linkify {
    color: var(--chops-link-color);
    text-decoration: none;
    font-weight: var(--chops-link-font-weight);
    font-family: var(--chops-font-family);
  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;
    justify-content: center;
    text-decoration: none;
    transition: filter 0.3s ease-in-out, box-shadow 0.3s ease-in-out;
  }
  a.button:hover, .button:hover {
    filter: brightness(95%);

    padding: var(--chops-button-padding);
  }

    display: block;
    margin-right: 4px;
  }
  chops-button.emphasized, a.button.emphasized, .button.emphasized {
    background: var(--chops-primary-button-bg);

  }
  textarea, select, input {
    box-sizing: border-box;
    font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for
  * accessibility because styles will not always line up with semantically
  * appropriate heading levels.

  .medium-heading {

          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;

          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;

          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }

        }
        .metadata-container {
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);

          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);

          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          z-index: 100;
        }
        .issue-header-container {

          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;
        }

          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;
          flex-grow: 1;

          min-height: 100%;

          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
        }
        mr-issue-metadata {
          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {
          border-left: var(--chops-normal-border);

          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

          }
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





When run setInterval method to multiple times calls requestFullScreen and append fullscreen element to another element to exit fullscreen mode,  interestingly after one single tap it able to fire onfullscreenchange event multiple times. 



<span class="line"><!---->When run setInterval method to multiple times calls requestFullScreen and append fullscreen element to another element to exit fullscreen mode,  interestingly after one single tap it able to fire onfullscreenchange event multiple times. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Surprisingly I notice when onfullscreenchange event fired multiple times in one tap it able to immediately hide (dismiss) the fullscreen notification while the browser is goes into fullscreen mode.



<span class="line"><!---->Surprisingly I notice when onfullscreenchange event fired multiple times in one tap it able to immediately hide (dismiss) the fullscreen notification while the browser is goes into fullscreen mode.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





- Chrome 100.0.4896.127 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome 100.0.4896.127 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)<!----></span>



<br>





- Chrome Beta 101.0.4951.41 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome Beta 101.0.4951.41 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)<!----></span>



<br>





- Chrome Dev 102.0.5005.22 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome Dev 102.0.5005.22 on Android 11 (Mi 9T)<!----></span>



<br>





- Chrome Dev 102.0.5005.22 on Android 10 (Android Emulator Pixel_2)



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome Dev 102.0.5005.22 on Android 10 (Android Emulator Pixel_2)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>



<br>





1. Visit attached testcase.html



<span class="line"><!---->1. Visit attached testcase.html<!----></span>



<br>





2. Tap anywhere on the page



<span class="line"><!---->2. Tap anywhere on the page<!----></span>



<br>





3. Tap again on the page



<span class="line"><!---->3. Tap again on the page<!----></span>



<br>





4. Browser goes into fullscreen without fullscreen notification toast



<span class="line"><!---->4. Browser goes into fullscreen without fullscreen notification toast<!----></span>



<br>

I'm not sure this is a meaningful security issue as scrolling on Android Chrome also hides the location bar (which is in some ways similar to this: a user gesture ends up with the site in a "fullscreen" mode without a location bar).



<span class="line"><!---->I'm not sure this is a meaningful security issue as scrolling on Android Chrome also hides the location bar (which is in some ways similar to this: a user gesture ends up with the site in a "fullscreen" mode without a location bar).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





+Android fullscreen folks to take a look. Assigning low severity for now, and FoundIn-96 as a suitable old version as I'm guessing this has been here for a while.



<span class="line"><!---->+Android fullscreen folks to take a look. Assigning low severity for now, and FoundIn-96 as a suitable old version as I'm guessing this has been here for a while.<!----></span>

> I'm not sure this is a meaningful security issue as scrolling on Android Chrome also hides the location bar (which is in some ways similar to this: a user gesture ends up with the site in a "fullscreen" mode without a location bar).



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; I'm not sure this is a meaningful security issue as scrolling on Android Chrome also hides the location bar (which is in some ways similar to this: a user gesture ends up with the site in a "fullscreen" mode without a location bar).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





According to WhatWG Fullscreen API Standard "User agents should ensure, e.g. by means of an overlay, that the end user is aware something is displayed fullscreen. User agents should provide a means of exiting fullscreen that always works and advertise this to the user. This is to prevent a site from spoofing the end user by recreating the user agent or even operating system environment when fullscreen"



<span class="line"><!---->According to WhatWG Fullscreen API Standard "User agents should ensure, e.g. by means of an overlay, that the end user is aware something is displayed fullscreen. User agents should provide a means of exiting fullscreen that always works and advertise this to the user. This is to prevent a site from spoofing the end user by recreating the user agent or even operating system environment when fullscreen"<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This only require tap gesture which normally doesn't hide the address bar. Regression started from 



<span class="line"><!---->Regression started from <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499<!----></a>





 where both 



<span class="line"><!----> where both <!----></span>



<br>





TWCDAImpl#enterFullscreenModeForTab and #fullscreenStateChangedForTab invoke the WCDA.enterFullscreenModeForTab(). On the second tap, full screen mode was already entered exited, followed by another (which is redundant and not quite correct in this case) request that puts Chrome in the fullscreen mode. again.



<span class="line"><!---->TWCDAImpl#enterFullscreenModeForTab and #fullscreenStateChangedForTab invoke the WCDA.enterFullscreenModeForTab(). On the second tap, full screen mode was already entered exited, followed by another (which is redundant and not quite correct in this case) request that puts Chrome in the fullscreen mode. again.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Needs a little more investigation as to why the notification toast is not brought up.



<span class="line"><!---->Needs a little more investigation as to why the notification toast is not brought up.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>

Basically, the javascript shoots enter/exit fullscreen request too fast. Chrome can't fire the internal events in order as expected. Notification toast is triggered by #onLayoutChange [1] after the fullscreen mode is entered, but a barrage of enter/exit requests don't let the event happen in time - they come at the end in a bunch, all of them stopped early by the if statement right above it checking if there is any actual height increase indicating we entered the fullscreen mode.



<span class="line"><!---->Basically, the javascript shoots enter/exit fullscreen request too fast. Chrome can't fire the internal events in order as expected. Notification toast is triggered by #onLayoutChange [1] after the fullscreen mode is entered, but a barrage of enter/exit requests don't let the event happen in time - they come at the end in a bunch, all of them stopped early by the if statement right above it checking if there is any actual height increase indicating we entered the fullscreen mode.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem happens when 1) fullscreen gets exited by one of the exit requests 2) fullscreen-state-change event occurs 3) As opposed to the intention of 



<span class="line"><!---->The problem happens when 1) fullscreen gets exited by one of the exit requests 2) fullscreen-state-change event occurs 3) As opposed to the intention of <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2516499<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 this turns on fullscreen mode again 3) now a series of #onLayoutChange event occurs but all early out as it doesn't see any height change (increase) at this point - bot old/new height are for fullscreen.



<span class="line"><!----> this turns on fullscreen mode again 3) now a series of #onLayoutChange event occurs but all early out as it doesn't see any height change (increase) at this point - bot old/new height are for fullscreen.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It can be fixed by limiting what fullscreen-state-change event does. Since this is introduced to invoke enter-fullscreen again even when it is already in fullscreen, in order to handle the fullscreen option that might have changed. It doesn't need to do anything when fullscreen was already exited.



<span class="line"><!---->It can be fixed by limiting what fullscreen-state-change event does. Since this is introduced to invoke enter-fullscreen again even when it is already in fullscreen, in order to handle the fullscreen option that might have changed. It doesn't need to do anything when fullscreen was already exited.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/fullscreen/FullscreenHtmlApiHandler.java;l=585;drc=755573e31718405aa13648d37c73e6dbe7dfe572



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/fullscreen/FullscreenHtmlApiHandler.java;l=585;drc=755573e31718405aa13648d37c73e6dbe7dfe572"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:chrome/android/java/src/org/chromium/chrome/browser/fullscreen/FullscreenHtmlApiHandler.java;l=585;drc=755573e31718405aa13648d37c73e6dbe7dfe572<!----></a>

Android: Process fullscreen state changes only when the mode is on



<span class="line"><!---->Android: Process fullscreen state changes only when the mode is on<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fullscreen state change event in Android is used to enter fullscreen



<span class="line"><!---->Fullscreen state change event in Android is used to enter fullscreen<!----></span>



<br>





mode again in order to deal with option-only changes even if the mode



<span class="line"><!---->mode again in order to deal with option-only changes even if the mode<!----></span>



<br>





is already on. This behavior, however, can be exploited to repeatedly



<span class="line"><!---->is already on. This behavior, however, can be exploited to repeatedly<!----></span>



<br>





trigger the mode on and off quickly, delay the layout change events,



<span class="line"><!---->trigger the mode on and off quickly, delay the layout change events,<!----></span>



<br>





which results in the fullscreen notification being suppressed.



<span class="line"><!---->which results in the fullscreen notification being suppressed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This CL modifies the behavior for fullscreen state change event. In



<span class="line"><!---->This CL modifies the behavior for fullscreen state change event. In<!----></span>



<br>





order to respect the intention of



<span class="line"><!---->order to respect the intention of<!----></span>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





crrev.com/c/2516499



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://crrev.com/c/2516499"><!---->crrev.com/c/2516499<!----></a>





 but also prevent



<span class="line"><!----> but also prevent<!----></span>



<br>





the potential issue at the same time, the flow proceeds only when



<span class="line"><!---->the potential issue at the same time, the flow proceeds only when<!----></span>



<br>





fullscreen mode is already on. It effectively stops the fullscreen mode



<span class="line"><!---->fullscreen mode is already on. It effectively stops the fullscreen mode<!----></span>



<br>





from being entered due to unintended state event changes.



<span class="line"><!---->from being entered due to unintended state event changes.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

<br>


    


        


      


        









*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward.
